                  <foreign lang="ar">صَفَرٌ</foreign>; (S, K;) and they say, (Msb,) one should only say, in speaking of them, <foreign lang="ar">شَهْرُ رَبِيعٍ الأَوَّلُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَهْرُ رَبِيعٍ الآخِرٌ</foreign>; (S, Msb, K;) [but in the margin of the copy of the S which I have here followed, I find it stated that in the handwriting of the author the former is <foreign lang="ar">شهر ربيعِ الاول</foreign> (with a single kesreh, and with no syll. sign to <foreign lang="ar">الاول</foreign>); and in another copy of the S I find <foreign lang="ar">شهرُ ربيع الاولِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَهرُ رَبيع الآخِر</foreign>;] with the addition of <foreign lang="ar">شهر</foreign>: but it is allowable to say also <foreign lang="ar">شَهْرُ رَبِيعِ الأَوَّلِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شَهْرُ رَبِيعِ الآخِرِ</foreign>: the word <foreign lang="ar">شهر</foreign> is necessarily added in order to discriminate between the months thus called and the season called <foreign lang="ar">ربيع</foreign>: Az says, the Arabs mention all the months without the word <foreign lang="ar">شهر</foreign> except the two months of <foreign lang="ar">ربيع</foreign> and the month of <foreign lang="ar">رَمَضَان</foreign>: and they say also <foreign lang="ar">شَهْرَا رَبِيعٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أَشْهُرُ رَبِيعٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شُهُورُ رَبِيعٍ</foreign>: (Msb:) these months were thus called because, when they received this name, they occurred in the season when the earth produced herbage. It has a twofold application also to seasons; <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الأَوَّلُ</foreign> being <hi rend="ital">The season in which the truffles and the blossoms come,</hi> (S, Msb, K,) and this is [also called] <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعُ الكَلَأِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the rabeea of the herbage,</hi> properly called <hi rend="ital">the spring of Arabia</hi>]; (S;) and <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الثَّانِى</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The season in which fruits ripen;</hi> (S, Msb, K;) [also called <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعُ الثِّمَارِ</foreign>;] but some people call this <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الأَوَّلُ</foreign>; (S, TA;) and the season which follows the winter, and in which the truffles and the blossoms come, they call <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الثَّانِى</foreign>; but all of them agree that the <foreign lang="ar">خَرِيف</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">autumn</hi>] is called <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ</foreign>: AHn says, the <hi rend="ital">two divisions of the winter</hi> [by which he means the <hi rend="ital">half-year commencing at the autumnal equinox</hi>] are called <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعَانِ</foreign>; the former being <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعُ المَآءِ وَالأَمْطَار ِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the rabeea of the water and the rains,</hi> in which the rain called <foreign lang="ar">الوَسْمِىّ</foreign>, which is termed the first of the rains, commences]; and the second being <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعُ النَّبَاتِ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعُ الكَلَأِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">the rabeea of the herbage</hi>], because the herbage therein attains to its last stage: and he adds, that <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعٌ</foreign> is applied by the Arabs to the whole <hi rend="ital">winter,</hi> [meaning, again, the <hi rend="ital">half-year commencing at the autumnal equinox,</hi>] because of the moisture, or rain: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">the year consists of six seasons;</hi> (so in the K; but in the S, “ and I heard Abu-l-Ghowth say, the Arabs make the year to be six seasons; ”) <hi rend="ital">two months thereof are called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الأَوَّلُ</foreign>; and two months, <foreign lang="ar">صَيْفٌ</foreign>; and two months, <foreign lang="ar">قَيْظٌ</foreign>; (S, K;) and <hi rend="ital">two months,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ربيع</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الثانى</foreign>, (so in a copy of the S,) or <foreign lang="ar">رَبِيعٌ الثّانى</foreign>, (so in another copy of the S, [but in the margin of this latter, I find it stated that in the handwriting of the author it is <foreign lang="ar">ربيعُ الثانى</foreign>, without tenween,]) or <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الثَّانِى</foreign>; (K;) and two months, <foreign lang="ar">خَرِيفٌ</foreign>; and two months, <foreign lang="ar">شِتَآءٌ</foreign>. (S, K.) Az relates, with respect to the seasons and divisions of the year, on the authority of Aboo-Yahyà Ibn-Kibáseh, who possessed very great knowledge thereof, that the year consists of four seasons; namely, <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الأَوَّلُ</foreign>, which the vulgar call <foreign lang="ar">الخَرِيفُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The autumn</hi>]; then <foreign lang="ar">الشِّتَآءُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the winter</hi>]; then <foreign lang="ar">الصَّيْفُ</foreign>, which is <foreign lang="ar">الرَّبِيعُ الآخِرُ</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">الثَّانِى</foreign>, i. e. <hi rend="ital">the spring</hi>]; then <foreign lang="ar">القَيْظُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">the summer,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hot season</hi>]: all this is what the Arabs in the desert say: <hi rend="ital">the</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ربيع</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">which is with the Persians the</hi>
